## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations and dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly time t, which is the standard state-space form of (nonlinear/forced/damped) oscillators. Common models include linear harmonic motion plus damping, nonlinear restoring forces (Duffing), self-excited oscillations (van der Pol/Rayleigh), and explicit time-dependent forcing/parametric excitation.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Undamped linear oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x (Hooke-law restoring acceleration)
- Linear viscous damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (mass-spring-damper in first-order state form)
- Constant bias / gravity offset: dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 (equilibrium shifted by constant acceleration)
- Coulomb (dry) friction damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * sign(v) (velocity-independent friction term)
- Quadratic drag damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v * Abs(v) (turbulent drag / high-speed damping)
- Nonlinear stiffness (Duffing, hardening/softening spring): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (cubic restoring force plus damping)
- General odd restoring force expansion: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5) - c3 * v (symmetric potential with higher-order terms)
- Simple pendulum (large-angle): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(x) - c1 * v (angular oscillator with sinusoidal restoring torque)
- Forced oscillator (additive drive): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (periodic external forcing)
- Forced Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (nonlinear stiffness with periodic drive)
- Parametric excitation (Mathieu-type): dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness)
- van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - x**2) * v - c2 * x (self-excited oscillation with nonlinear damping)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * (c1 - v**2) * v - c2 * x (nonlinear damping primarily in velocity)
- Conservative nonlinear oscillator from potential: dv_dt = -(c0 * x + c1 * sin(c2 * x) + c3 * x**3) (effective force as negative gradient of a nonlinear potential)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Restoring-force symmetry: if the oscillator is symmetric about equilibrium, dv_dt is typically an odd function of x (e.g., -x, -x - x**3, -sin(x)) and has no even powers of x.
- Dissipation signature: any term that is odd in v and tends to oppose motion (e.g., -c*v, -c*sign(v), -c*v*Abs(v)) indicates damping; its presence implies mechanical energy decreases without forcing.
- Autonomous vs driven: explicit dependence on t (sin/cos, time-varying coefficients) signals external forcing or parametric excitation; absence of t suggests an autonomous system.
- Amplitude-dependent frequency: nonlinear stiffness terms (x**3, x**5, sin(x)) imply the oscillation frequency shifts with amplitude (hardening/softening behavior).
- Limit-cycle indicator: nonlinear damping of the form (c0 - x**2)*v or (c0 - v**2)*v produces self-sustained oscillations that converge to a stable cycle rather than decaying to rest.
- Dry-friction behavior: sign(v) terms produce stick–slip and non-smooth acceleration near v = 0, often visible as piecewise-linear velocity decay.
- Drag regime identification: v*Abs(v) damping implies strong high-speed dissipation; linear -v damping implies low-Reynolds viscous losses.
- Equilibrium shift: constant terms in dv_dt (or a nonzero linear term c0*x plus bias) indicate the equilibrium position is not at x = 0 (e.g., gravity-loaded spring).
- Coupled nonlinearities: mixed products like x**2*v or x*v*Abs(v) (if they appear) often represent state-dependent damping or geometric nonlinearities beyond simple spring-damper models.

GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - c1*beta*v - beta*exp(-Abs(v))*v
Candidate formulas: 50

GT (fixed) is:
\[
f(t,v)=0.66863216766915\sin(t)\;-\;0.0585985712804097\,v^3\;-\;0.716668620096812\,v\;-\;0.358334310048406\,v\,e^{-|v|}
\]
Key structural requirements:
- Depends **only on** \(t\) and \(v\) (no \(x\) dependence at all).
- Has a **sinusoid in \(t\)** (can be represented as a cosine with phase shift).
- Has polynomial terms \(v^3\) and \(v\).
- Has the **non-polynomial damping** term \(v e^{-|v|}\) (crucial).
- No constant offset term.

Now check candidates.

General eliminations that apply to many:
- Any candidate with unavoidable \(x\) terms like “\(+x\)” (not multiplied by a free constant) cannot match GT because GT has no \(x\) dependence.
- Any candidate lacking a \(v e^{-|v|}\) term (or something algebraically identical) cannot match GT, because \(v e^{-|v|}\) is not representable by polynomials, \(v|v|\), \(v/(|v|+1)\), etc., for all real \(v\).
- Any candidate with only \( \exp(c t)\) (time exponential) cannot reproduce \(\sin(t)\) for all \(t\).

GT: F0*sin(t) - alpha*v**c0 - c1*beta*v - beta*exp(-Abs(v))*v
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT:** `-0.0585985712804097*v**3 - 0.716668620096812*v - 0.358334310048406*v*exp(-Abs(v)) + 0.66863216766915*sin(t)`

The GT has these basis functions:
1. `v**3` (with coefficient)
2. `v` (with coefficient)
3. `v*exp(-Abs(v))` (with coefficient)
4. `sin(t)` (with coefficient)

No `x` dependence, no `exp(c*t)` terms, no `cos(t)` (though `sin(t)` can be written as `cos(t - π/2)`).

Key observations:
- GT has NO `x` dependence at all
- GT has `v*exp(-Abs(v))`, NOT `v*Abs(v)`
- GT has `sin(t)`, which equals `cos(t - π/2)`

**Critical issue:** Almost all candidates contain `v*Abs(v)` instead of `v*exp(-Abs(v))`. These are fundamentally different functions - `v*Abs(v)` is a polynomial-like function (equals `v|v|`), while `v*exp(-Abs(v))` involves an exponential decay. These are NOT equivalent for any constant choice.

Let me check if any candidate has `v*exp(-Abs(v))` or something equivalent... None do.

Let me also check candidates without `v*Abs(v)` to see if they might work differently:

- **Candidates 42, 43, 48, 50**: Have `v**3`, `v`, and extra `v` terms but no `v*exp(-Abs(v))`. They have `v*Abs(v)` missing but also lack `v*exp(-Abs(v))`.

Wait, let me re-examine. Candidates 42, 43, 48, 50 have terms like `c5*v` or `c6*v` instead of `v*Abs(v)`. But they still don't have `v*exp(-Abs(v))`.

**For ALL candidates:** None contain the term `v*exp(-Abs(v))`. The GT requires this specific basis function. Since `v*exp(-Abs(v))` is linearly independent from `v`, `v**3`, `v*Abs(v)`, `sin(t)`, `cos(t)`, `x`, `exp(c*t)`, etc., no linear combination of the basis functions present in any candidate can reproduce `v*exp(-Abs(v))`.

By the principle of linear independence of basis functions (Rule 3), none of these candidates can match the GT.

Let me verify this for every candidate:

Candidates 1-50: All lack `v*exp(-Abs(v))` as a basis function. This term cannot be reproduced by any combination of `v`, `v**3`, `v*Abs(v)`, `x`, `exp(c*t)`, `sin(t)`, `cos(t)`, `x^(1/5)*exp(c*t)`, `log(...)`, `1/(|x|+1)^2`, etc.
